<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_2">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_World_Cup_hosts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 28 May 2015, media covering the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_corruption_case" title="2015 FIFA corruption case">2015 FIFA corruption case</a> reported that high-ranking officials from the South African bid committee had secured the right to host the World Cup by paying US $10 million in bribes to then-FIFA Vice President <a href="/wiki/Jack_Warner_(football_executive)" title="Jack Warner (football executive)">Jack Warner</a> and to other FIFA Executive Committee members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 June 2015, FIFA executive <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Blazer" title="Chuck Blazer">Chuck Blazer</a>, having co-operated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI">FBI</a> and the Swiss authorities, confirmed that he and the other members of FIFA's executive committee were bribed in order to promote the South African 1998 and 2010 World Cups. Blazer stated, "I and others on the Fifa executive committee agreed to accept bribes in conjunction with the selection of South Africa as the host nation for the 2010 World Cup." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 June 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> had received the most votes, but <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> was awarded the tournament instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_FIFA_World_Cup"><a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_World_Cup_hosts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 2014 FIFA World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_bids" title="2014 FIFA World Cup bids">2014 FIFA World Cup bids</a></div>
<p>Bids:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="720" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/33px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/43px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 2x" width="22"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a></li>
</ul>
<p>FIFA continued its continental rotation procedure by earmarking the 2014 World Cup for <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>. FIFA initially indicated that it might back out of the rotation concept,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> but later decided to continue it through the 2014 host decision, after which it was dropped.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> had expressed interest in hosting the 2014 World Cup,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> but withdrew undertaking the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2011 FIFA U-20 World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> also expressed interest in hosting the World Cup. <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">CONMEBOL</a>, the South American Football Federation, indicated their preference for Brazil as a host.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Brazil was the only nation to submit a formal bid when the official bidding procedure for CONMEBOL member associations was opened in December 2006, as by that time, Colombia, Chile and Argentina had already withdrawn, and Venezuela was not allowed to bid.</p>
<p>Brazil made the first unopposed bid since the initial selection of the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 FIFA World Cup</a> (when Colombia was selected as host, but later withdrew for financial problems). The FIFA Executive Committee confirmed it as the host country on 30 October 2007 by a unanimous decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>

<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/FIFA_receives_eleven_bids_for_2018_and_2022_World_Cups" title="wikinews:FIFA receives eleven bids for 2018 and 2022 World Cups">FIFA receives eleven bids for 2018 and 2022 World Cups</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>FIFA announced on 29 October 2007 that it will no longer continue with its continental rotation policy, implemented after the 2006 World Cup host selection. The newest host selection policy is that any country may bid for a World Cup, provided that their continental confederation has not hosted either of the past two World Cups. For the <a href="/wiki/2018_and_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bids" title="2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bids">2018 World Cup bidding process</a>, this meant that bids from Africa and South America were not allowed.</p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2018_and_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bids" title="2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bids">2022 World Cup bidding process</a>, this meant that bids from South America and Europe were not allowed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-press_conference_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-press_conference-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_fifa_rotation_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_fifa_rotation-26">[26]</a></sup> Also, FIFA formally allowed joint bids once more (after they were banned in 2002), due to there being only one organizing committee per joint bid, unlike Korea/Japan, which had two different organizing committees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blatter_announces_what.27s_to_come_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blatter_announces_what.27s_to_come-27">[27]</a></sup> Countries that announced their interest included Australia, England, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, Japan, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, Russia, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, United States, the joint bid of Spain and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and the joint bid of Belgium and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-press_conference_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-press_conference-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iberian_threat_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Iberian_threat-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Australia_Drops_Out_of_Race_to_Host_2018_World_Cup_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Australia_Drops_Out_of_Race_to_Host_2018_World_Cup-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The hosts for both World Cups were announced by the FIFA Executive Committee on 2 December 2010. Russia was selected to host the 2018 FIFA World Cup, making it the first time that the World Cup will be hosted in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and making it the biggest country geographically to host the World Cup. <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> was selected to host the 2022 FIFA World Cup, making it the first time a World Cup will be held in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and the second time in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. Also, the decision made it the smallest country geographically to host the World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifa20182022_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-fifa20182022-30">[30]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accusations_of_bribery">Accusations of bribery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_World_Cup_hosts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Accusations of bribery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concerns_and_controversies_over_the_2022_FIFA_World_Cup" title="Concerns and controversies over the 2022 FIFA World Cup">Concerns and controversies over the 2022 FIFA World Cup</a></div>
<p>Before the vote, allegations of bribery resulted in the suspension of two FIFA Executive Committee members, reducing the number of voters to 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-temarii_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-temarii-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2011, allegations of corruption within the <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> senior officials raised questions over the legitimacy of the World Cup being held in Qatar. According to then vice-President <a href="/wiki/Jack_Warner_(football_executive)" title="Jack Warner (football executive)">Jack Warner</a>, an email has been publicised about the possibility that Qatar 'bought' the 2022 World Cup through bribery via <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Hammam" title="Mohammed bin Hammam">Mohammed bin Hammam</a> who was president of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">Asian Football Confederation</a> at the time. Qatar's officials in the bid team for 2022 have denied any wrongdoing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>A whistleblower, revealed to be Phaedra Almajid, alleged that several African officials were paid $1.5 million by Qatar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> She later retracted her claims of bribery, stating she had fabricated them in order to exact revenge on the Qatari bid team for relieving her of her job with them. She also denied being put under any pressure to make her retraction. FIFA confirmed receiving an email from her which stated her retraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 June 2014, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> claimed to have obtained documents including e-mails, letters and bank transfers which allegedly proved that Bin Hammam had paid more than US$5 million to football officials to support the Qatar bid. Bin Hamman and all those accused of accepting bribes denied the charges <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>More suspicions emerged in March 2014 when it was discovered that <a href="/wiki/Jack_Warner_(football_executive)" title="Jack Warner (football executive)">Jack Warner</a>, who was made to leave his post as president of <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> in disgrace, and his family were paid almost $2 million from a firm linked to Qatar's successful campaign. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI">FBI</a> is investigating Warner and his alleged links to the Qatari bid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2026_FIFA_World_Cup"><a href="/wiki/2026_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2026 FIFA World Cup">2026 FIFA World Cup</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_World_Cup_hosts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: 2026 FIFA World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2026_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2026 FIFA World Cup">2026 FIFA World Cup</a></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> bid for the 2026 World Cup is probable, with Canada, USA, and Mexico the most likely nations to bid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Under FIFA rules as of 2013, the 2026 Cup cannot be in either Europe or Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> leaving an African bid, a North American bid, a South American bid or an Oceania bid as other possible options.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> However, at the FIFA Congress held on 30 May 2015 in Zürich, that decision changed, prohibiting only bids from Asia and allowing everyone else to bid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The bidding process was originally scheduled to start in 2015, with the appointment of hosts scheduled for the FIFA Congress on 10 May 2017 in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifa20150320_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-fifa20150320-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> On 10 June 2015, FIFA announced that the bid process for the 2026 FIFA World Cup was postponed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> However, following the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Council" title="FIFA Council">FIFA Council</a> meeting on 10 May 2016, a new bid schedule was announced for May 2020 as the last in a four-phase process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-process_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-process-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>CONCACAF member federations (Canada, Mexico, United States) are favoured to host the 2026 World Cup for the first time since 1994 World Cup. Also, FIFA's president Infantino will consider the option for triple co-hosting by Canada, Mexico and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap-cbc_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap-cbc-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> On 14 October 2016, FIFA said it will accept CONCACAF triple tournament-sharing bid by Canada, Mexico and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to CONCACAF president, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Montagliani" title="Victor Montagliani">Victor Montagliani</a>, there would be a possibility of a joint bid between <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> to host the 2026 FIFA World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Confirmed 2026 Bids:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2030_FIFA_World_Cup">2030 FIFA World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_World_Cup_hosts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 2030 FIFA World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Six early bids for the 2030 FIFA World Cup have been proposed, with a collective bid from the members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luke.2C_Hunt_The_Diplomat.2C_17_Nov_2013_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Luke.2C_Hunt_The_Diplomat.2C_17_Nov_2013-61">[61]</a></sup> a proposed bid by the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Chile" title="Football Federation of Chile">Football Federation of Chile</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emol.com_8-6-14_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-emol.com_8-6-14-62">[62]</a></sup> a proposed joint bid from <a href="/wiki/Uruguay%E2%80%93Argentina_2030_FIFA_World_Cup_bid" title="Uruguay–Argentina 2030 FIFA World Cup bid">Uruguay and Argentina</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mondial-de-football_Jan_2016_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-mondial-de-football_Jan_2016-63">[63]</a></sup> a proposed bid from <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telam.com.ar_11_Nov_2014_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-telam.com.ar_11_Nov_2014-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ELTIEMPO.com_27_Nov_2014_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-ELTIEMPO.com_27_Nov_2014-65">[65]</a></sup> a proposed bid from <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph.uk_14_Jan_2017_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.uk_14_Jan_2017-66">[66]</a></sup> and a proposed joint bid from <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nzherald_13_April_2015_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-nzherald_13_April_2015-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soceroos.com.au_13_April_2015_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-soceroos.com.au_13_April_2015-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Uruguay–Argentina bid would coincide with the centennial anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/1930_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1930 FIFA World Cup">first FIFA World Cup</a> in Uruguay and the bicentennial of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Uruguay_of_1830" title="Constitution of Uruguay of 1830">first Constitution of Uruguay</a>.</p>
<p>England FA vice president <a href="/wiki/David_Gill_(executive)" title="David Gill (executive)">David Gill</a> has proposed that his country could potentially bid for 2030, provided that the bidding process is made more transparent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espn.co.uk_31_March_2015_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-espn.co.uk_31_March_2015-69">[69]</a></sup> "England is one of few countries that could stage even a 48-nation event in its entirety, while Football Association chief executive Martin Glenn made it clear earlier this year bidding for 2030 was an option."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph.uk_14_Jan_2017_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.uk_14_Jan_2017-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unconfirmed 2030 Bids:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_country_performances">Host country performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_World_Cup_hosts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Host country performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/National_team_appearances_in_the_FIFA_World_Cup" title="National team appearances in the FIFA World Cup">National team appearances in the FIFA World Cup</a></div>
<p>It is widely considered that <a href="/wiki/Home_advantage" title="Home advantage">home advantage</a> is common in the World Cup, with the host team usually performing above average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[70]</a></sup> Of the eight countries that have won the tournament, only Brazil and Spain were not champions at home, and both England and France had their only titles as hosts.</p>
<p>Further, Sweden got to its only final as hosts of the 1958 tournament, and only the Swedes and Brazilians finished as runner-up in home soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[71]</a></sup> The host country reached the semifinals thirteen times in twenty tournaments, and both Chile and South Korea had their only finishes on the top four at home. Only South Africa in 2010 managed to not go past the group stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[72]</a></sup></p>

<li><b><a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup"><i>2018</i></a>:</b> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/15px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/30px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="15"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a></span> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Russian_Football_Union" title="Russian Football Union">RFS</a>)</small></li>
